Faqir and Miskin: Definitions and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Definitions and intra-Hanafi dispute on the categories of faqir and miskin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between faqir and miskin according to the Hanafi school and explain the practical difference between Abu Hanifa's and Abu Yusuf's views on their categorization.

Core Idea
Faqir does not beg, miskin does — a distinction that changes distributions in wills, not in zakat.

What makes a 'poor person' different from a 'needy person'? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi definitions of faqir and miskin and examines an intra-Hanafi dispute over whether they form one or two categories. Although both are eligible for zakat, the categorization affects how bequests are divided in wills and endowments.

Guided Path
1
Define the terms
According to the passage, al-faqir is one who possesses the least thing and does not ask people; al-miskin possesses nothing and asks.
From al-Yanabee' as cited in the text.
2
Understand the dispute
Abu Hanifa considers them two separate categories (صنفان); Abu Yusuf considers them one category (صنف واحد).
Reported by Qadi Khan.
3
Identify the practical consequence
In zakat, both are eligible, so no difference. In wills, if one bequeaths to a person and to fuqara and masakin, Abu Hanifa divides the bequest into three equal shares; Abu Yusuf divides it into two halves.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.
4
Note the tarjih
The text does not give a definitive tarjih, but Abu Hanifa's view is more widely relied upon in the school.
Implicit in school practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والفقيرُ : مَن له أدنى شيء. والمسكينُ : مَن لا شيء له. قال في «الينابيع»: الفقير هو الذي لا يسأل الناس، ولا يطوف على الأبواب، والمسكين هو الذي يسأل الناس، ويطوف على الأبواب. فإن قيل: البداية بالفقراء: دليل على أنهم أحوج. قلنا: إنما بدأ بهم؛ لأنهم لا يسألون فالاهتمام بهم مقدَّم على من يسأل. وهذا الخلاف لا تظهر له فائدة في الزكاة؛ لأنه يجوز الدفع إلى جميعهم، وإنما تظهر في الوصايا والأوقاف. وهل الفقراء والمساكين صنف واحد، أو صنفان؟ قال قاضي خان: صنفان عند أبي حنيفة، وقال أبو يوسف: صنف واحد. وفائدته : إذا أوصى بثلث ماله لفلان وللفقراء والمساكين: فعلى قول أبي حنيفة: الثلث بينهم أثلاثاً، وعلى قول أبي يوسف: نصفان: نصفه لفلان ونصفه للفقراء والمساكين.
Al-faqir: one who possesses the least thing. Al-miskin: one who possesses nothing. He said in al-Yanabee': Al-faqir is the one who does not ask people and does not go around to doors; al-miskin is the one who asks people and goes around to doors. If it is said: Starting with the poor (fuqara) indicates that they are more needy. We say: He only started with them because they do not ask, so caring for them takes precedence over those who ask. This difference has no benefit in zakat because it is permissible to pay to all of them, but it appears in wills and endowments. Are the fuqara and masakin one category or two? Qadi Khan said: Two categories according to Abu Hanifa, and Abu Yusuf said: One category. Its benefit: If someone bequeaths one-third of his property to Zayd and to the fuqara and masakin, then according to Abu Hanifa the third is divided equally among the three; according to Abu Yusuf, half is for Zayd and half for the fuqara and masakin.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage presents definitions and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The commentator first defines the terms based on al-Yanabee': al-faqir is one who possesses the bare minimum and does not beg; al-miskin is one who has nothing and begs. Although the Quran begins with 'fuqara', the commentator explains that does not imply they are more needy; rather, they are mentioned first because they do not ask, so they are more deserving of attention. This difference in definition has no practical effect in zakat because both categories are eligible and can be given to any of them. However, it matters in wills and endowments where distributions are specified. The main dispute is whether they are distinct categories (صنفان) or one (صنف واحد). According to Qadi Khan, Abu Hanifa holds that they are two separate categories, while Abu Yusuf holds they are one. The practical consequence is shown in a will: if one bequeaths one-third to Zayd and to the fuqara and masakin, on Abu Hanifa's view the third is split into three equal parts (one for Zayd, one for fuqara, one for masakin); on Abu Yusuf's view, it is split into two halves (one for Zayd, one for the combined fuqara and masakin). The text does not specify the mufta bihi position, but typically the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school is that they are two categories, as stated by Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
الفقير (al-faqīr): One who possesses the minimum of wealth (or less than nisab) and does not beg.
المسكين (al-miskīn): One who possesses nothing and begs.
صنف (ṣinf): Category or class. In this context, whether الفقراء and المساكين form one or two categories.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical difference between Abu Hanifa's and Abu Yusuf's views on الفقراء and المساكين?
A) In zakat distribution.
B) In the amount of zakat given.
C) In wills and endowments.
D) In the eligibility of the collector.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi distinction between faqir and miskin is behavioral, and it matters in wills not in zakat.

The Zakat Collector: Payment, Loss, and Hashimi Exemption
Rulings on the zakat collector's payment and eligibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the zakat collector's compensation, the effect of lost funds, and the prohibition of giving zakat to a Hashimi collector.

Core Idea
The collector's payment is for work, not fixed price; loss forfeits his fee but not the payer's obligation.

This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira explains key rulings concerning the zakat collector (al-ʿāmil). It details how the imam determines the collector's compensation according to his work, what happens if the collected funds are lost, and a special restriction regarding descendants of the Prophet (Hashimis). Understanding these rules ensures proper implementation of zakat administration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the collector's role and compensation basis
Recognize that the collector is an appointee of the imam, and his payment is not a fixed price but rather a reasonable amount determined by the imam based on the work done.
The compensation covers the collector and his assistants.
2
Analyze the effect of loss of zakat funds
If the collected zakat money perishes or is lost in the collector's hands, his right to payment is forfeited. However, the loss does not invalidate the zakat of the payers – their obligation is fulfilled.
This balances the collector's responsibility with the payers' security.
3
Examine the Hashimi prohibition
A Hashimi (descendant of the Prophet) cannot receive any portion of zakat, even as payment for collection, to keep them free from the suspicion of impurity. They may be compensated from non-zakat funds if appointed as collector.
This is a special honor for the Prophet's lineage.
4
Distinguish the ruling for non-Hashimi wealthy collectors
A non-Hashimi collector may receive zakat payment even if he is wealthy, because his wealth does not grant him the same elevated status as a Hashimi.
Wealth does not disqualify a non-Hashimi from this category.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (والعاملُ يَدفعُ إليه الإمامُ إِن عَمِلَ بقدر عَمَلِه): أي يعطيه ما يكفيه وأعوانه بالمعروف غير مقدر بالثمن. والعامل هو : الساعي الذي نَصَبَه الإمام على أخذ الصدقات. ولو هلك المال في يد العامل، أو ضاع: سقط حقه، وأجزأ عن الزكاة عن المؤدين. ولا يجوز أن يُعطى العامل الهاشمي من الزكاة شيئاً؛ تنزيهاً لقرابة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن شبهة الوسخ. ويجوز لغير الهاشمي ذلك وإن كان غنياً؛ لأن الغني لا يوازي الهاشمي في استحقاق الكرامة. فإن جُعِلَ الهاشمي عاملاً، وأعطي من غير الزكاة: فلا بأس به.
He said: 'And the collector: the imam gives to him if he works, according to his work.' That is, he gives him what suffices him and his assistants in a reasonable manner, not measured by price. The collector is the agent appointed by the imam to collect the alms. If the money perishes in the collector's hand or is lost, his right (to payment) is forfeited, and it suffices for the zakat of the payers. It is not permissible to give the Hashimi collector anything from the zakat, as a means of keeping the relatives of the Messenger of Allah free from the suspicion of filth. It is permissible for a non-Hashimi even if he is wealthy, because a wealthy person does not compare to a Hashimi in deserving honor. If a Hashimi is appointed as a collector and is paid from other than zakat, there is no problem.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage states rulings regarding the zakat collector (العامل). The collector is appointed by the Imam to collect zakat. His payment is determined by the Imam based on his work, without a fixed price, but sufficient for him and his assistants. If the collected zakat is lost or perishes in the collector's hand, his right to payment is forfeited, but the payers' zakat obligation is still fulfilled (the loss does not invalidate their payment). A significant ruling: a Hashimi (descendant of the Prophet) cannot be given any portion of zakat as payment for collecting, to avoid any suspicion of impurity (since zakat is considered 'the filth of people'). However, a non-Hashimi may be given payment even if he is wealthy, because a wealthy non-Hashimi does not have the same elevated status as a Hashimi. If a Hashimi is appointed as a collector, he may be paid from other funds (non-zakat sources).

Key Terms
العامل (al-ʿāmil): The person appointed by the Imam to collect zakat.
الهاشمي (al-hāshimī): A descendant of the Prophet from the Hashim clan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if the zakat money is lost in the collector's hand?
A) The collector must replace it from his own wealth.
B) The collector forfeits his right to payment, but the payers' zakat is valid.
C) The zakat becomes invalid and must be repaid.
D) The Imam must pay the collector from the state treasury.

Key Takeaway
The zakat collector's payment is work-based; loss forfeits his fee, and Hashimis cannot receive zakat even as collectors.

Dispute on whether fuqara and masakin are one or two categories in zakat
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the classification of zakat recipients

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on the classification of fuqara and masakin, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to a will distribution scenario.

Core Idea
The classification of fuqara and masakin as one or two categories changes the distribution of zakat and bequests.

Zakat distribution requires identifying the correct categories of recipients. The Quran mentions both fuqara and masakin, but scholars differ on whether they are distinct. This passage from Fatawa Qadi Khan records an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and shows how a seemingly subtle difference in classification affects actual inheritance calculations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
Determine the exact point of disagreement: Are fuqara and masakin separate categories or one? State Abu Hanifa's view (two) and Abu Yusuf's view (one).
The text does not provide proofs; focus on the practical difference.
2
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah) given in the text: in a will where a third is left to a named person, fuqara, and masakin, the division changes based on the categorization.
Calculate the number of shares: Abu Hanifa: three shares; Abu Yusuf: two shares.
3
Identify the mufta bihi position
Determine which view is relied upon for fatwa. The text implies Abu Hanifa's view is the majority and mufta bihi.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference; both positions are valid within the school.
4
Understand why it matters in fiqh
Reflect on why such a classification is important beyond this specific will example. It affects zakat distribution, charity priorities, and legal drafting.
Precision in categorization ensures Shariah compliance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهل الفقراء والمساكين صنف واحد، أو صنفان؟ قال قاضي خان: صنفان عند أبي حنيفة، وقال أبو يوسف: صنف وفائدته : إذا أوصى بثلث ماله لفلان وللفقراء والمساكين: فعلى قول أبي حنيفة: الثلث بينهم أثلاثاً، وعلى قول أبي يوسف: نصفان: نصفه لفلان ونصفه للفقراء والمساكين.
And are the poor and needy one category or two? Qadi Khan said: two categories according to Abu Hanifa, and Abu Yusuf said: one category. Its benefit: if one bequeaths a third of his wealth to so-and-so and to the poor and needy: then according to Abu Hanifa the third is divided among them in thirds, and according to Abu Yusuf: halves: half for so-and-so and half for the poor and needy.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the classification of the poor (fuqara) and needy (masakin) as recipients of zakat. While the Quran mentions both in Surah At-Tawbah (9:60), scholars differ on whether they are distinct categories. Abu Hanifa holds they are two separate categories, each entitled to a share. Abu Yusuf treats them as one category. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) appears in wills: if someone bequeaths a third of his wealth to a named individual and to the poor and needy, according to Abu Hanifa the third is divided into three equal shares (one for the individual, one for the poor, one for the needy), while according to Abu Yusuf it is divided into two halves. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa. This dispute is recorded by Qadi Khan in his Fatawa, which is a later source (fatawa mutakhkhirin).

Key Terms
الفقراء (al-fuqara): The poor: those who have no wealth or income sufficient for basic needs.
المساكين (al-masakin): The needy: those who have some wealth but not enough for basic needs.
صنف (sinf): Category or class (of zakat recipients).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone bequeaths a third of their wealth to 'Zaid, the poor, and the needy' what is the distribution according to Abu Hanifa?
A) A third of the third to Zaid, a third to the poor, and a third to the needy
B) Half to Zaid and half to the poor and needy combined
C) All to the poor and needy, Zaid excluded
D) The entire third goes to Zaid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon view treats the poor (fuqara) and needy (masakin) as separate categories, affecting both zakat distribution and will calculations.

The Zakat Worker: Compensation and the Hashimi Exclusion
Commentary on the worker's compensation and Hashimi rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on paying the zakat worker from zakat funds and identify when a Hashimi worker may receive compensation.

Core Idea
A zakat worker is paid from zakat even if rich, but a Hashimi worker is excluded out of honor.

In this lesson, we examine the rulings for the zakat worker (al-‘āmil), whom the Imam appoints to collect zakat. The commentary explains his compensation, the effect of loss of collected wealth, and the special prohibition for Hashimi workers. Understanding these rules ensures correct distribution and respect for the Prophet’s lineage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the worker
Define al-‘āmil as the zakat collector appointed by the Imam. Note that his role is to collect and distribute zakat.
2
Determine compensation
The worker is given what suffices him and his assistants in a reasonable manner, without a fixed amount. This is considered a wage (ujrah) in one respect and a charity (sadaqah) in another.
Because it is a wage, he may receive it even if rich; because it is a charity, Hashimis are excluded.
3
Analyze loss of wealth
If the collected zakat perishes or is lost in the worker’s hand, his right to compensation lapses, but the zakat obligation of the payers is still fulfilled.
The worker bears the risk, but the donor’s obligation is discharged.
4
Apply the Hashimi prohibition
A Hashimi worker cannot be given any zakat funds. If a Hashimi is appointed, he must be paid from non-zakat sources.
This is to honor the Prophet’s family and avoid any suspicion of impurity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
* قوله: (والعاملُ يَدفعُ إليه الإمامُ إِن عَمِلَ بقدر عَمَلِه): أي يعطيه ما يكفيه وأعوانه بالمعروف غير مقدر بالثمن. والعامل هو : الساعي الذي نَصَبَه الإمام على أخذ الصدقات. وأجزأ عن ولو هلك المال في يد العامل، أو ضاع: سقط حقه، الزكاة عن المؤدين. ولا يجوز أن يُعطى العامل الهاشمي من الزكاة شيئاً؛ تنزيهاً لقرابة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن شبهة الوسخ. ويجوز لغير الهاشمي ذلك وإن كان غنياً؛ لأن الغني لا يوازي الهاشمي في استحقاق الكرامة. فإن جُعِلَ الهاشمي عاملاً، وأعطي من غير الزكاة: فلا بأس به.

وفي الرقاب : يُعان المكاتبون في فَك رقابهم . والغارمُ : مَن لزمه دَيْنٌ. وفي سبيل الله : مُنقَطَعُ الغُزَاة . - ثم الذي يأخذه العامل أجرةً من وجه، حتى يجوز له مع الغنى، وصدقةً من وجه، حتى لا يجوز للعامل الهاشمي، تنزيهاً له عنها. قوله: (وفي الرقاب : يُعان المكاتبون في فك رقابهم)، إلا مكاتب الهاشمي، فإنه لا يُعطى منها شيئاً. بخلاف مكاتب الغني إذا كان كبيراً، وأما إذا كان صغيراً: فلا يجوز. فإن عجز المكاتب وقد دفعت إليه الزكاة: يطيب لمولاه الغني أكلها. وكذا إذا دفعت الزكاة إلى الفقير، ثم استغنى والزكاة باقية في يده: يطيب له أكلها. قوله: (والغارمُ مَن لزمه دين أي يحيط بماله، أو لا يملك نصاباً فاضلاً عن دينه. وكذا إذا كان له دين على غيره : لم يكن به غنياً، سواء كان نصاباً أو أكثر ؛ لأنه لم يكن بذلك غنياً. * قوله : (وفي سبيل الله : منقطَعُ الغزاة): هذا عند أبي يوسف. وعند محمد : منقطع الحاج. وفائدة الخلاف: في الوصية.
* His saying: (And the worker, the Imam gives to him if he works, in proportion to his work): meaning he gives him what suffices him and his assistants in a reasonable manner without fixing a price. The worker is the collector whom the Imam appoints to collect zakat. And if the wealth perishes in the worker's hand, or is lost, his right lapses, and the zakat is fulfilled for the payers. It is not permissible to give the Hashimi worker anything from the zakat, to keep the relatives of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) free from suspicion of impurity. It is permissible for a non-Hashimi even if he is rich, because a rich person does not match the Hashimi in entitlement to honor. If a Hashimi is appointed as a worker and is paid from other than zakat, it is fine.

And regarding slaves: mukatabs are assisted in freeing themselves. And the indebted: is one who is bound by a debt. And in the way of Allah: stranded travelers. - Then what the worker takes is a wage in one respect, so it is permissible for him despite wealth, and a charity in another respect, so it is not permissible for the Hashimi worker, to keep him away from it. His saying: (And regarding slaves: mukatabs are assisted in freeing their necks), except the mukatab of a Hashimi, for he is not given anything from it. Unlike the mukatab of a rich person if he is an adult; if he is a minor, it is not permissible. If the mukatab becomes unable (to pay) and zakat was given to him, it becomes permissible for his rich master to consume it. Likewise, if zakat is given to a poor person, then he becomes rich while the zakat remains in his hand, it is permissible for him to consume it. His saying: (And the indebted is one who is bound by a debt) meaning it encompasses his wealth, or he does not possess a nisab surplus to his debt. Likewise, if he has a debt owed to him by someone else, he is not thereby rich, whether the debt is a nisab or more; because he is not rich by that. * His saying: (And in the way of Allah: stranded travelers): this according to Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad: stranded pilgrims. The benefit of the difference is in wills.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the categories of zakat recipients as outlined in the matn of Al-Quduri. It provides detailed rulings for four categories: the worker ('amil), the slaves (mukatabun), the indebted (gharimun), and those in the way of Allah (fi sabil Allah).

1. **The Worker ('Amil):** The worker is appointed by the Imam to collect zakat. He is given compensation sufficient for himself and his assistants, without a fixed amount. If the collected wealth is lost before distribution, the worker's right to compensation is lost, but the zakat obligation of the payers is still fulfilled. A Hashimi (descendant of the Prophet) cannot be given zakat as a worker, to avoid any suspicion of impurity. A non-Hashimi worker may be given even if he is rich, because the honor of the Hashimi lineage is higher than wealth. If a Hashimi is employed as a worker, he may be paid from other sources.

2. **The Slaves (Riqab/Mukatabun):** Only mukatab slaves (those who have a contract of manumission) are assisted from the zakat funds to help them free themselves. However, the mukatab of a Hashimi master is not given zakat. A mukatab of a rich master may be given if he is an adult; if he is a minor, it is not allowed. If the mukatab later becomes unable to pay his contract, the zakat given becomes lawful for his rich master to consume. Similarly, if a poor recipient becomes rich after receiving zakat, the zakat remains lawful for him.

3. **The Indebted (Gharim):** An indebted person is one whose debt envelops his wealth, or he does not possess a nisab (minimum threshold) beyond his debt. He is considered eligible for zakat even if he has a debt owed to him by others, regardless of whether that debt equals a nisab or more, because he is not presently rich.

4. **In the Way of Allah (Fi Sabil Allah):** There is an intra-Hanafi difference. According to Abu Yusuf, it refers to stranded travelers (those cut off from their wealth on a journey). According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, it refers to stranded pilgrims. The practical consequence appears in wills: if someone bequeaths for 'fi sabil Allah', the distribution depends on which interpretation is followed.

Throughout, there is a consistent principle: the Hashimi (descendant of the Prophet) is exempt from receiving zakat out of honor, but may receive from other funds.

Key Terms
العامل (al-'amil): The zakat worker appointed by the Imam to collect zakat.
الهاشمي (al-hashimi): A descendant of Hashim, from the tribe of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it prohibited to give zakat to a Hashimi worker?
A) Because Hashimis are always rich
B) To keep the Prophet's relatives free from suspicion of impurity
C) Because they are not eligible for any charitable payments
D) Because they do not work as zakat collectors

Key Takeaway
A zakat worker may be paid from zakat even if rich, but a Hashimi worker must be paid from non-zakat funds to honor the Prophet's lineage.

Assisting Mukatab Slaves from Zakat
Commentary on the riqab category: conditions for giving to mukatab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the conditions for giving zakat to a mukatab slave and identify the exceptions for the mukatab of a Hashimi master.

Core Idea
Mukatab slaves are assisted from zakat, but not the mukatab of a Hashimi master, and only adult mukatabs of rich masters qualify.

The second recipient category is 'riqab' (slaves), which in Hanafi fiqh is specifically for mukatab slaves—those who have a contract of manumission. This lesson clarifies who qualifies, the Hashimi exception, and what happens if the mukatab later becomes unable to pay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
In the context of zakat, 'riqab' refers specifically to mukatab slaves (those with a contract to earn their freedom).
Non-mukatab slaves are not eligible.
2
State the general rule
Mukatab slaves are given from zakat to help them fulfill their manumission contract.
This is a form of assisting in freeing necks.
3
Apply the Hashimi exception
The mukatab of a Hashimi master is not given anything from zakat, just as the Hashimi himself is prohibited from receiving zakat.
The prohibition extends to the benefit reaching the Hashimi indirectly.
4
Consider the rich master case
If the mukatab's master is rich, the mukatab may be given zakat only if he is an adult; a minor mukatab is not eligible.
The reasoning is that a minor cannot effectively manage the contract.
5
Handle subsequent inability
If after receiving zakat the mukatab becomes unable to pay his contract (e.g., he gives up), the zakat given becomes lawful for his rich master to consume.
This prevents waste and mirrors the rule for a poor recipient who later becomes rich.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
* قوله: (والعاملُ يَدفعُ إليه الإمامُ إِن عَمِلَ بقدر عَمَلِه): أي يعطيه ما يكفيه وأعوانه بالمعروف غير مقدر بالثمن. والعامل هو : الساعي الذي نَصَبَه الإمام على أخذ الصدقات. وأجزأ عن ولو هلك المال في يد العامل، أو ضاع: سقط حقه، الزكاة عن المؤدين. ولا يجوز أن يُعطى العامل الهاشمي من الزكاة شيئاً؛ تنزيهاً لقرابة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن شبهة الوسخ. ويجوز لغير الهاشمي ذلك وإن كان غنياً؛ لأن الغني لا يوازي الهاشمي في استحقاق الكرامة. فإن جُعِلَ الهاشمي عاملاً، وأعطي من غير الزكاة: فلا بأس به.

وفي الرقاب : يُعان المكاتبون في فَك رقابهم . والغارمُ : مَن لزمه دَيْنٌ. وفي سبيل الله : مُنقَطَعُ الغُزَاة . - ثم الذي يأخذه العامل أجرةً من وجه، حتى يجوز له مع الغنى، وصدقةً من وجه، حتى لا يجوز للعامل الهاشمي، تنزيهاً له عنها. قوله: (وفي الرقاب : يُعان المكاتبون في فك رقابهم)، إلا مكاتب الهاشمي، فإنه لا يُعطى منها شيئاً. بخلاف مكاتب الغني إذا كان كبيراً، وأما إذا كان صغيراً: فلا يجوز. فإن عجز المكاتب وقد دفعت إليه الزكاة: يطيب لمولاه الغني أكلها. وكذا إذا دفعت الزكاة إلى الفقير، ثم استغنى والزكاة باقية في يده: يطيب له أكلها. قوله: (والغارمُ مَن لزمه دين أي يحيط بماله، أو لا يملك نصاباً فاضلاً عن دينه. وكذا إذا كان له دين على غيره : لم يكن به غنياً، سواء كان نصاباً أو أكثر ؛ لأنه لم يكن بذلك غنياً. * قوله : (وفي سبيل الله : منقطَعُ الغزاة): هذا عند أبي يوسف. وعند محمد : منقطع الحاج. وفائدة الخلاف: في الوصية.
* His saying: (And the worker, the Imam gives to him if he works, in proportion to his work): meaning he gives him what suffices him and his assistants in a reasonable manner without fixing a price. The worker is the collector whom the Imam appoints to collect zakat. And if the wealth perishes in the worker's hand, or is lost, his right lapses, and the zakat is fulfilled for the payers. It is not permissible to give the Hashimi worker anything from the zakat, to keep the relatives of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) free from suspicion of impurity. It is permissible for a non-Hashimi even if he is rich, because a rich person does not match the Hashimi in entitlement to honor. If a Hashimi is appointed as a worker and is paid from other than zakat, it is fine.

And regarding slaves: mukatabs are assisted in freeing themselves. And the indebted: is one who is bound by a debt. And in the way of Allah: stranded travelers. - Then what the worker takes is a wage in one respect, so it is permissible for him despite wealth, and a charity in another respect, so it is not permissible for the Hashimi worker, to keep him away from it. His saying: (And regarding slaves: mukatabs are assisted in freeing their necks), except the mukatab of a Hashimi, for he is not given anything from it. Unlike the mukatab of a rich person if he is an adult; if he is a minor, it is not permissible. If the mukatab becomes unable (to pay) and zakat was given to him, it becomes permissible for his rich master to consume it. Likewise, if zakat is given to a poor person, then he becomes rich while the zakat remains in his hand, it is permissible for him to consume it. His saying: (And the indebted is one who is bound by a debt) meaning it encompasses his wealth, or he does not possess a nisab surplus to his debt. Likewise, if he has a debt owed to him by someone else, he is not thereby rich, whether the debt is a nisab or more; because he is not rich by that. * His saying: (And in the way of Allah: stranded travelers): this according to Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad: stranded pilgrims. The benefit of the difference is in wills.
Source pages p. 221

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the categories of zakat recipients as outlined in the matn of Al-Quduri. It provides detailed rulings for four categories: the worker ('amil), the slaves (mukatabun), the indebted (gharimun), and those in the way of Allah (fi sabil Allah).

1. **The Worker ('Amil):** The worker is appointed by the Imam to collect zakat. He is given compensation sufficient for himself and his assistants, without a fixed amount. If the collected wealth is lost before distribution, the worker's right to compensation is lost, but the zakat obligation of the payers is still fulfilled. A Hashimi (descendant of the Prophet) cannot be given zakat as a worker, to avoid any suspicion of impurity. A non-Hashimi worker may be given even if he is rich, because the honor of the Hashimi lineage is higher than wealth. If a Hashimi is employed as a worker, he may be paid from other sources.

2. **The Slaves (Riqab/Mukatabun):** Only mukatab slaves (those who have a contract of manumission) are assisted from the zakat funds to help them free themselves. However, the mukatab of a Hashimi master is not given zakat. A mukatab of a rich master may be given if he is an adult; if he is a minor, it is not allowed. If the mukatab later becomes unable to pay his contract, the zakat given becomes lawful for his rich master to consume. Similarly, if a poor recipient becomes rich after receiving zakat, the zakat remains lawful for him.

3. **The Indebted (Gharim):** An indebted person is one whose debt envelops his wealth, or he does not possess a nisab (minimum threshold) beyond his debt. He is considered eligible for zakat even if he has a debt owed to him by others, regardless of whether that debt equals a nisab or more, because he is not presently rich.

4. **In the Way of Allah (Fi Sabil Allah):** There is an intra-Hanafi difference. According to Abu Yusuf, it refers to stranded travelers (those cut off from their wealth on a journey). According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, it refers to stranded pilgrims. The practical consequence appears in wills: if someone bequeaths for 'fi sabil Allah', the distribution depends on which interpretation is followed.

Throughout, there is a consistent principle: the Hashimi (descendant of the Prophet) is exempt from receiving zakat out of honor, but may receive from other funds.

Key Terms
المكاتب (al-mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of manumission with his master, requiring payment of a sum.
الهاشمي (al-hashimi): A descendant of Hashim, from the tribe of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mukatab slave becomes unable to pay his contract after receiving zakat, what happens to the zakat?
A) The zakat must be returned to the payers.
B) The zakat becomes permissible for the rich master to consume.
C) The zakat is invalid and must be given again.
D) The zakat is given to another poor person.

Key Takeaway
Mukatab slaves are eligible for zakat except those owned by a Hashimi; and if the master is rich, the mukatab must be an adult.

beginner
5 min
The Indebted (Gharim): Eligibility for Zakat
Commentary on the indebted (gharim) and the treatment of debts owed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define who qualifies as a gharim (indebted person) for zakat and explain why debts owed to the person do not make him rich.

Core Idea
A debtor is eligible for zakat if his debt exceeds or consumes his wealth; even if others owe him money, he is not considered wealthy.

The third category is the indebted (al-ghārim). This lesson clarifies the Hanafi definition: a person burdened by debt that either exceeds his wealth or leaves him with less than a nisab. Importantly, having a debt owed to him by others does not render him rich, because that debt is not accessible cash.

Guided Path
1
Define the gharim
Al-ghārim is one who is bound by a debt (dīn) that encompasses his wealth, meaning his liabilities exceed his assets, or he has no surplus nisab after paying the debt.
He is eligible even if he owns property that is encumbered.
2
Consider debts owed to him
If the gharim has a debt owed to him by someone else, that debt does not make him rich, even if it equals or exceeds a nisab.
The rationale: he cannot immediately access that money; it is not liquid wealth.
3
Apply the condition
The condition for receiving zakat as gharim is that after subtracting the debt from his assets, he does not possess a nisab of surplus wealth.
This is a distinct category from the poor (faqir) or needy (miskin), though there is overlap.

Fi Sabil Allah: Two Hanafi Interpretations
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the meaning of fi sabil Allah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi views on the meaning of 'fi sabil Allah' in zakat and state the practical consequence in wills.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf says it means stranded travelers; Muhammad says it means stranded pilgrims; the difference appears in wills.

The final category 'fi sabil Allah' (in the way of Allah) has an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. Abu Yusuf interprets it as stranded travelers (munqati' al-ghuzah), while Muhammad al-Shaybani interprets it as stranded pilgrims (munqati' al-hajj). This lesson explores both views and their practical effect in the context of a will.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
The Quranic category 'fi sabil Allah' is one of the eight categories of zakat recipients. The Hanafi school specifies it as stranded travelers (or pilgrims).
This is a restrictive interpretation compared to other schools.
2
State Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf says it refers to stranded travelers (munqati' al-ghuzah), i.e., those cut off from their wealth while on a legitimate journey.
These are not necessarily warriors but any traveler in need.
3
State Muhammad's view
Muhammad al-Shaybani says it refers to stranded pilgrims (munqati' al-hajj), specifically those on the pilgrimage who have run out of funds.
This is a narrower interpretation.
4
Identify the practical consequence
The difference manifests in wills: if a person bequeaths something 'fi sabil Allah', the distribution depends on which interpretation is followed.
No tarjih (preference) is given in the text; both views are recorded.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

B) It affects the distribution of wills
C) It affects who can collect zakat
D) It affects the amount of zakat due

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two interpretations of 'fi sabil Allah' – stranded travelers (Abu Yusuf) or stranded pilgrims (Muhammad) – with practical impact on wills.

Conditions for Zakat Recipients: The Riqab Category
Explains the fiqh of giving zakat to mukatab slaves with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a mukatab slave is eligible to receive zakat from the riqab category and apply these conditions to determine the validity of such payments.

Core Idea
Zakat for riqab is specifically for mukatab slaves, with restrictions on Hashimi, child, and wealthy adult recipients.

Zakat has eight categories of recipients, one of which is 'riqab' (slaves). This passage clarifies that only mukatab slaves (those in a contract to buy their freedom) qualify. However, not every mukatab is eligible—certain conditions and exceptions apply. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly disbursing zakat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category and its definition
The passage begins by stating that 'riqab' refers to helping mukatab slaves. Recognize that this category is specifically for slaves who have a contract of manumission (mukatab).
2
List the conditions for eligibility
From the text, extract the conditions: the recipient must be a mukatab, must not be a Hashimi, and if an adult, wealth is not a barrier; but a child mukatab is not eligible.
3
Note the exceptions and prohibitions
The passage explicitly excludes Hashimi mukatab and child mukatab. Also note that a wealthy adult mukatab is permissible, contrary to the general rule that zakat is for the needy.
The exclusion of Hashimi is due to honor, as zakat is considered impure for them.
4
Understand the consequences of subsequent changes
If the mukatab becomes unable to pay his contract after receiving zakat, the master may lawfully consume the zakat. Similarly, if a poor recipient becomes rich, he may keep the zakat.
These rulings are based on the principle that zakat ownership is established at receipt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الرقاب : يُعان المكاتبون في فَك رقابهم .
قوله: (وفي الرقاب : يُعان المكاتبون في فك رقابهم)، إلا مكاتب الهاشمي، فإنه لا يُعطى منها شيئاً.
بخلاف مكاتب الغني إذا كان كبيراً، وأما إذا كان صغيراً: فلا يجوز. فإن عجز المكاتب وقد دفعت إليه الزكاة: يطيب لمولاه الغني أكلها. وكذا إذا دفعت الزكاة إلى الفقير، ثم استغنى والزكاة باقية في يده: يطيب له أكلها.
And regarding slaves (riqab): the mukatab are helped in freeing their necks. He said: (And regarding slaves: the mukatab are helped in freeing their necks), except a Hashimi mukatab, for he is given nothing of it. Contrary to the wealthy mukatab if he is an adult, but if he is a child: it is not permissible. If the mukatab becomes unable and zakat was paid to him, it is lawful for his wealthy master to consume it. Likewise, if zakat was paid to a poor person, then he became rich with the zakat remaining in his hand: it is lawful for him to consume it.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the riqab category of zakat recipients. The author first states the matn: 'And regarding slaves: the mukatab are helped in freeing their necks.' Then the commentary explains the details. The category of riqab is specifically for mukatab slaves (those who have contracted with their masters to purchase their freedom). Zakat may be given to them to help them become free. However, there are exceptions: a mukatab who is a Hashimi cannot be given zakat, as zakat is deemed impure for them out of honor. Also, if the mukatab is wealthy (i.e., has means) but is an adult, it is permissible to give to him; if he is a child, it is not permissible. If the mukatab becomes unable to pay after receiving zakat, the zakat is lawful for his wealthy master to consume. Similarly, if a poor person receives zakat and later becomes rich, the zakat remains lawful for him; he need not return it.

Key Terms
الرقاب (ar-riqāb): Literally 'necks'; in zakat, a category for helping slaves free themselves.
المكاتب (al-mukātab): A slave who has contracted to purchase his freedom in installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A Hashimi mukatab
B) A wealthy adult mukatab
C) A child mukatab
D) A mukatab who has already paid his contract

Key Takeaway
Zakat paid to a mukatab slave is valid if he is not Hashimi and not a child; subsequent changes in his status do not affect the validity.

Definition and Conditions of the Gharim (Indebted Zakat Recipient)
Defines gharim and conditions for receiving zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the gharim and state the conditions under which an indebted person is eligible to receive zakat according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A gharim is eligible for zakat when debts exceed assets or leave no surplus nisab.

Zakat has eight categories of recipients, one of which is the gharim (indebted person). However, not every person with debt qualifies. The Hanafi school sets clear conditions that determine when a debtor is considered truly needy and thus deserving of zakat funds. This lesson unpacks those conditions from the classical text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its legal definition
The passage defines 'gharim' literally as 'one for whom a debt is binding.' Understand that this is a technical term in zakat law.
2
Extract the primary condition for eligibility
The condition is that the debt 'encompasses his wealth' or leaves him without a surplus nisab. That is, his debts exceed his total assets, or after paying debts, his remaining wealth is below the nisab threshold.
3
Analyze the secondary condition regarding debts owed to him
If someone is owed a debt by another person, that receivable is not counted as wealth for determining zakat eligibility. Even if the receivable equals or exceeds nisab, the person is still considered gharim because he does not have liquid access to that wealth.
This is a Hanafi position; other schools may differ.
4
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Scenario: A person has assets worth 1000, debts of 1200, and is owed 500 by a friend. He has no other wealth. According to the Hanafi conditions, he is a gharim because his debts exceed his assets (1200 > 1000), and the receivable is not considered wealth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والغارمُ : مَن لزمه دَيْنٌ.
قوله: (والغارمُ مَن لزمه دين أي يحيط بماله، أو لا يملك نصاباً فاضلاً عن دينه.
وكذا إذا كان له دين على غيره : لم يكن به غنياً، سواء كان نصاباً أو أكثر ؛ لأنه لم يكن بذلك غنياً.
And the gharim (indebted) is one for whom a debt is binding. He said: (And the gharim is one for whom a debt is binding), that is, it encompasses his wealth, or he does not possess nisab surplus to his debt. Also if he has a debt owed to him by another: he is not considered wealthy by it, whether it is nisab or more; because he is not wealthy by that.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage defines the gharim category of zakat recipients. According to the commentary, a gharim is someone whose debts exceed his wealth, or whose remaining wealth after debts is below the nisab threshold. Additionally, if someone is owed a debt by another person, that debt does not count as wealth in determining his eligibility; he is still considered poor because he lacks liquid assets. This is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
الغارم (al-ghārim): One who is indebted; as a zakat recipient, one whose debts exceed his assets or leaves him without nisab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) No, because he is not wealthy by it
C) Yes, always
D) No, but only if the debtor is rich

Key Takeaway
A gharim qualifies for zakat only when his debts exceed his wealth or leave him with no surplus nisab, and receivables do not count as wealth.

Zakat Recipients: Fi Sabil Allah and Ibn al-Sabil
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fi sabil Allah and definition of ibn al-sabil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi interpretations of 'fi sabil Allah' and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) in wills.

Core Idea
Fi sabil Allah in zakat: Abu Yusuf says warriors, Muhammad says pilgrims – the difference matters in a will.

The Quran mentions eight categories of zakat recipients, including 'fi sabil Allah' and 'ibn al-sabil'. In this lesson, we delve into the Hanafi understanding of these two terms. The passage reveals an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding who qualifies as 'fi sabil Allah'. This disagreement is not just theoretical – it has a direct practical consequence in the execution of wills (wasiyyah). Understanding this nuance is essential for applying zakat correctly and fulfilling bequests according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two recipient categories
The passage addresses two of the eight asnaf (categories) of zakat: 'fi sabil Allah' and 'ibn al-sabil'. Note how each is defined in the text.
'Fi sabil Allah' is defined differently by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
2
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute on fi sabil Allah
The matn says 'fi sabil Allah' means those cut off from the ghuzat (warriors). The commentary adds that this is Abu Yusuf's view, while Muhammad interprets it as those cut off from the hujjaj (pilgrims). Understand the basis of each interpretation.
Both views are within the Hanafi school, not against it.
3
Locate the thamarah al-khilaf
The text says 'and the benefit of the difference is in the will' (wa fa’idat al-khilaf fi al-wasiyyah). This means the dispute affects how a bequest made for 'fi sabil Allah' must be executed.
Focus on the practical consequence: who receives the bequest.
4
Understand the ruling on ibn al-sabil
The passage defines ibn al-sabil as a traveler stranded far from his wealth, without access to funds or a lender. He is given zakat only enough to return home, not more. If he already has provisions, he is not eligible.
This is a unanimous Hanafi position, not disputed.
5
Summarize the conditions for each recipient
Synthesize the conditions: for fi sabil Allah, the recipient must be cut off from his group (warriors or pilgrims). For ibn al-sabil, the traveler must be in need and unable to obtain his own money.
The conditions ensure zakat reaches the truly needy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي سبيل الله : مُنقَطَعُ الغُزَاة .
* قوله : (وفي سبيل الله : منقطَعُ الغزاة): هذا عند أبي يوسف.
وعند محمد : منقطع الحاج.
وفائدة الخلاف: في الوصية.

وابن السبيل : مَن كان له مال في وطنه وهو في مكان آخر لا شيء له فيه، ولا يجد من يدينه : فيُعطى من الزكاة لحاجته.
وإنما يأخذ ما يكفيه إلى وطنه، لا غير.
وسمي ابن السبيل : لأنه ملازم للسفر والسبيل: الطريق، فنُسب إليه.
ولو كان معه ما يوصله إلى بلده من زادٍ وحمولة: لم يجز أن يعطى من الزكاة؛ لأنه غير محتاج.
And in the cause of Allah: those cut off from the ghuzat (warriors). He said: (And in the cause of Allah: those cut off from the warriors): this is according to Abu Yusuf. And according to Muhammad: those cut off from the pilgrims. And the benefit of the difference is in the will. And the son of the road (traveler) is one who has wealth in his homeland, and he is in another place having nothing of it, and he cannot find anyone to lend to him: so he is given from the zakat for his need. And he only takes what suffices him to his homeland, not more. And he is called 'ibn al-sabil' because he is attached to travel, and 'sabil' is the path, so he is attributed to it. And if he has with him what would get him to his country of provisions and mount, it is not permissible to give him from the zakat because he is not needy.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage covers two categories: 'fi sabil Allah' and 'ibn al-sabil'. For 'fi sabil Allah', the matn says it is for those cut off from the ghuzat (warriors). The commentary reveals an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Imam Abu Yusuf, it refers to warriors who are cut off from their army. According to Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, it refers to pilgrims who are cut off. The practical difference appears in wills (wasiyyah): if someone bequeaths for 'fi sabil Allah', Abu Yusuf gives it to warriors, Muhammad to pilgrims. As for 'ibn al-sabil' (the traveler), the matn defines him as one who has wealth in his homeland but is away without access, and no one to lend. He is given zakat sufficient to return home, no more. If he already has provisions and transport, he is not eligible.

Key Terms
في سبيل الله (fī sabīl Allāh): Literally 'in the cause of Allah'; as a zakat category, interpreted as cut-off warriors or pilgrims.
ابن السبيل (ibn al-sabīl): The wayfarer; a traveler stranded away from his wealth.
منقطع الغزاة/الحاج (munqata' al-ghuzāh/al-hājj): Those cut off from warriors/pilgrims; the qualifying condition for fi sabil Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) In the distribution of annual zakat
B) In the execution of wills
C) In the definition of traveler
D) In the permissibility of giving to the wealthy

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, 'fi sabil Allah' includes both cut-off warriors and cut-off pilgrims, a disagreement that directly impacts wills, while 'ibn al-sabil' is strictly limited to the stranded traveler's return expenses.

Zakat Distribution and Prohibition for Dhimmis
States permissibility of single-category zakat and prohibition for dhimmis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on giving zakat to one category versus all eight, and identify the ruling on giving zakat to a dhimmi.

Core Idea
Zakat may be given to any single category; zakat to a dhimmi is invalid, though voluntary charity is permitted.

Zakat is prescribed for eight categories, but does the payer have to cover all? The Hanafi school gives flexibility. Also, who can receive zakat? The dhimmi is excluded from obligatory zakat but not from voluntary charity. Let's examine the textual basis and the inter-madhhab difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the passage
The passage covers (1) permissibility of giving zakat to one or all categories, and (2) prohibition of giving zakat to a dhimmi.
Note the contrast with voluntary charity which is allowed by consensus.
2
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute on distribution
The Hanafi position: it is permissible to give all zakat to one category. Imam al-Shafi'i requires distribution to at least three from each category. Understand the opposing proofs.
The Hanafi rely on the apparent meaning of Quran 9:60 and companion practice.
3
Apply the ruling on dhimmis
The text explicitly forbids giving zakat to a dhimmi. Voluntary charity is allowed by consensus.
Other obligatory charities like fitr and expiations are disputed, as per the footnote.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهذه جهات الزكاة، وللمالك أن يدفع إلى كل واحد منهم، وله أن يقتصر على صنف واحد .
* قوله: (فهذه جهات الزكاة، وللمالك أن يدفع إلى كل واحد منهم، وله أن يقتصر على صنف واحد).
وقال الشافعي : لا يجوز إلا أن يصرف إلى ثلاثة من كل صنف. * قوله: (ولا يجوز أن تُدفع الزكاة إلى ذمي).
ويجوز دفع صدقة التطوع إليه، إجماعاً.
واختلفوا في صدقة الفطر والنذور، والكفارات:
(1) ينظر تفصيل ذلك في المجموع ١٨٥/٦.
These are the channels of zakat, and the owner (payer) may give to each one of them, and he may confine himself to one type. He said: (These are the channels of zakat, and the owner may give to each of them, and he may confine himself to one type). And al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible unless he distributes to three from each type. He said: (And it is not permissible to give zakat to a dhimmi). And it is permissible to give voluntary charity to him, by consensus. And they differed regarding zakat al-fitr, vows, and expiations. (1) See the details in al-Majmu' 6/185.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues. First, the zakat payer may distribute his zakat to all eight categories or confine it to a single category. This is the Hanafi position, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds that one must give to at least three recipients from each category. Second, zakat cannot be given to a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen). However, voluntary charity (sadaqat al-tatawwu') may be given to them by consensus. Other obligatory charities like zakat al-fitr, vows, and expiations are subject to scholarly difference; the footnote refers to al-Majmu' for details.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmī): A non-Muslim under the protection of the Islamic state.
جهات الزكاة (jihāt al-zakāh): The eight categories eligible to receive zakat as listed in Quran 9:60.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Permissible only if he is poor
D) Permissible with the permission of the imam

Key Takeaway
Zakat may be given to a single category, but never to a dhimmi; voluntary charity is always permissible.

Zakat Recipients: Confining to One Category
Ruling on confining zakat to one category

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on confining zakat to one recipient category and explain the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Zakat may be given to a single category or person; the eight categories are options, not mandatory targets.

The passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah clarifies that the payer of zakat has flexibility in distribution. You may give to all eight categories or to just one. This flexibility contrasts with the Shafi'i position, which requires distribution to at least three individuals from each category. Understanding this difference helps you appreciate the Hanafi school's emphasis on practicality and the payer's discretion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on distribution
Find the statement that the owner may confine zakat to a single category (صنف واحد). This is the core Hanafi position.
The text says 'وله أن يقتصر على صنف واحد'.
2
Locate the opposing view
Identify the reference to Imam al-Shafi'i's position: he requires distribution to at least three individuals from each category.
Opposing school: Shafi'i.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Explain why the Hanafi school allows this flexibility. The categories are merely eligible recipients; the aim is fulfilling the obligation, not necessarily reaching many individuals.
The text does not give a detailed response, but the ruling implies discretion.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: giving all zakat to one poor person is valid in the Hanafi school but invalid in the Shafi'i school unless the payer also gives to at least three others from each category, which may be impractical.
This affects how a Hanafi mufti advises on zakat distribution.

And the evidence that tamlik is not realized in shrouding the dead is that if a wolf ate the dead person, the shroud belongs to the shroud-giver, not to the heir. Likewise in al-Nihayah. And likewise a debt of a dead person should not be paid with it. And water cisterns should not be built with it, and wells should not be dug with it. And it is not permissible unless a poor person takes possession of it, or a guardian or agent takes possession for him; because it is a transfer of ownership, and possession is necessary in it, and therefore it is not permissible to feed it by way of ibaha (permission). And if he pays a debt of a living person with it: if it was without his command, it is not permissible; and if it was with his command, it is permissible if he is poor, and it is as if he gave it as charity to him, and the receiver is like an agent for him in receiving the charity to him.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is an expanded commentary on the chapter of who may receive zakat from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. It begins by defining 'ibn al-sabil' (the wayfarer) as someone with wealth in his homeland but stranded elsewhere without resources. He is given only what suffices to return home, not more. The text then states that the zakat payer may distribute to one or multiple of the eight categories. A dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i is noted: Shafi'i requires distribution to at least three individuals from each category, while the Hanafi position allows giving to any number, even one. Next, the prohibition of giving zakat to a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen) is affirmed, but voluntary charity is allowed by consensus. There is an intra-Hanafi difference regarding other obligatory charities (fitr, nadhr, kaffarat): according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two), it is permissible but less rewardable; Abu Yusuf prohibits it by analogy with zakat. For a musta'min harbi (non-Muslim with temporary protection), all obligatory charity is prohibited by consensus, but voluntary charity is allowed. The passage then explains that zakat cannot be used to build mosques, shroud the dead, pay debts of the dead, or build water facilities because these lack tamlik (transfer of ownership), which is a necessary condition (rukn) for zakat distribution. The evidence: if a wolf eats a shrouded corpse, the shroud goes to the shroud-giver, not the heir, showing ownership stays with the giver. Finally, the text discusses the requirement of possession (qabd) by the poor person, a guardian, or an agent; mere permission to eat is invalid. Paying the debt of a living person is only valid if he ordered it and is poor, as the payer becomes a proxy.

Key Terms
صنف (sinf): Category of eligible zakat recipients, one of the eight groups mentioned in Quran 9:60.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum number of categories a zakat payer must distribute to?
A) All eight
B) At least three
C) One category is sufficient
D) At least two

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows giving all zakat to a single category or even a single individual, providing flexibility for the payer.

Zakat to Non-Muslims: Dhimmi and Musta'min
Ruling on giving zakat to non-Muslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving zakat to a dhimmi and a musta'min, and explain the intra-Hanafi difference on other obligatory sadaqat.

Core Idea
Zakat cannot be given to a dhimmi or musta'min; voluntary charity is allowed to both by consensus.

This passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah addresses the eligibility of non-Muslims for zakat. It clearly prohibits giving zakat to a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen) and a musta'min (temporarily protected non-Muslim). However, voluntary charity can be given to them by consensus. There is also an intra-Hanafi difference on whether other obligatory sadaqat (fitr, nadhr, kaffarat) may be given to a dhimmi. Understanding these distinctions is essential for proper zakat distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on zakat to dhimmi
The text states clearly: 'ولا يجوز أن تُدفع الزكاةُ إِلى ذِمِّي' (it is not permissible to give zakat to a dhimmi).
This is a definitive prohibition.
2
Differentiate voluntary charity
Note that voluntary charity (صدقة التطوع) is permissible to a dhimmi by consensus (إجماعاً).
This shows the distinction between obligatory and voluntary.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi difference
For other obligatory sadaqat (fitr, nadhr, kaffarat), Abu Hanifa and Muhammad allow giving to a dhimmi but say giving to poor Muslims is better; Abu Yusuf prohibits it by analogy with zakat.
This is an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Apply the ruling to musta'min
For a musta'min harbi (non-Muslim with temporary protection), zakat and all obligatory charity are prohibited by consensus; voluntary charity is allowed.
Consensus on this point.

The Pillar of Tamlik: Conditions for Zakat Distribution
Explanation of tamlik requirement for zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why tamlik (transfer of ownership) is a pillar of zakat and apply it to identify permissible and impermissible uses of zakat funds.

Core Idea
Zakat requires actual transfer of ownership to a poor person; it cannot be spent on buildings, shrouds, or debts of the dead.

The passage from al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah concludes by discussing the essential condition (rukn) of tamlik in zakat distribution. The author explains that zakat funds cannot be used to build mosques, shroud the dead, pay debts of the dead, or dig wells because these uses do not involve transferring ownership to a poor person. The proof is given: if a wolf eats a shrouded corpse, the shroud belongs to the giver, not the heir, showing ownership was not transferred. This lesson clarifies the practical boundaries of zakat spending and the importance of qabd (possession) by the recipient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition of tamlik
The text states that tamlik (transfer of ownership) is the pillar (الركن) of zakat. It then lists prohibited uses due to lack of tamlik.
Words: 'لانعدام التمليك منه، وهو الركن'.
2
Analyze the evidence (shroud and wolf)
The commentator provides a proof: if a wolf eats a corpse that was shrouded with zakat, the shroud remains owned by the giver, not the heir, showing tamlik did not occur.
This is a dalil naqli (transmitted evidence) from the commentary.
3
List prohibited uses
Build mosque, shroud dead, pay dead person's debt, build water cisterns, dig wells. All lack tamlik.
Also cannot be given as ibaha (mere permission to eat).
4
Understand the exception: paying debt of a living person
If a living poor person orders the payer to pay his debt, it is valid because the payer becomes like a proxy (وكيل) for the poor person, and tamlik is achieved through the debt payment.
Condition: the debtor must be poor.

التمليك (al-tamlik): Transfer of ownership to the recipient, a necessary condition (rukn) for zakat.
القبض (al-qabd): Taking possession of the zakat by the recipient or his agent.
الإباحة (al-ibaha): Permission to use without transfer of ownership.

The Pillar of Tamlik: Invalid Uses of Sadaqah
Listing invalid uses of sadaqah due to lack of tamlik

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which charitable acts are invalid as sadaqah because they lack tamlik (ownership transfer) and state the underlying reason.

Core Idea
Sadaqah requires tamlik; building mosques, shrouding dead, and freeing slaves do not transfer ownership.

This section of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira emphasizes that the essence of sadaqah is transferring ownership to a recipient. The author lists several common charitable expenditures—building a mosque, shrouding a dead person, paying off a deceased person's debt, building water stations, digging wells, and buying a slave to free—and rules that these are not valid uses of sadaqah. The key is that none of these actions give ownership of the charity to a living individual. Understanding this condition is essential for properly discharging sadaqah obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited acts
List the acts that the text prohibits using sadaqah for: building a mosque, shrouding a deceased person, paying the debt of a deceased person, building water stations, digging wells, buying a slave to free.
These are all common charitable acts, but they are invalid for sadaqah.
2
Understand the reason: absence of tamlik
The text explains that the common factor is the absence of tamlik (ownership transfer). The essence (rukn) of sadaqah is tamlik.
Tamlik means giving ownership to a specific recipient.
3
Examine the proof for shrouding
The wolf example: if a wolf eats the corpse, the shroud belongs to the one who shrouded, not the heir, proving ownership was not transferred to the deceased.
This shows that the deceased cannot own property, so tamlik is impossible.
4
Apply the principle to other acts
Each act similarly lacks tamlik: building a mosque benefits the public without giving ownership; freeing a slave is isqat al-milk (relinquishing ownership) not tamlik.
The principle is consistent: any use that does not transfer ownership to a living person is invalid.
5
Conclude on valid sadaqah
Valid sadaqah requires a poor person to take possession (qabd) either directly or through a guardian/agent.
Qabd is a necessary condition for completion of the transfer.

ويجوز صرف صدقة التطوع إليه.
قوله: (ولا يُبنى بها مسجد، ولا يُكفَّن بها ميت) ؛ لانعدام التمليك منه، وهو الركن.
والدليل على أن التمليك لا يتحقق في تكفين الميت: أن الذئب لو أكل الميت: يكون الكفن للمكفِّن، لا للوارث. كذا في «النهاية».
وكذا لا يُقضى بها دين ميت.
- ولا تُبنى بها السقايات، ولا تُحفر بها الآبار.
ولا يجوز إلا أن يقبضها فقير، أو يقبضها له ولي، أو وكيل؛ لأنها تمليك، ولا بد فيها من القبض، ولهذا لا يجوز إطعامها بطريق الإباحة.
وإن قضى بها دين حي: إن كان بغير أمره: لا يجوز، وإن كان بأمره: جاز إذا كان فقيراً، وكأنه تصدق بها عليه ويكون القابض كالوكيل له في قبض الصدقة إليه.
ولا يُشترى بها رقبةٌ تُعتق .
ولا تُدفع إلى غني.
قوله: (ولا) يُشترى بها رقبةٌ تُعتَق) ؛ لأن العتق إسقاط الملك، وليس بتمليك.
* قوله: (ولا تُدفع إلى غني ) ؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «لا تحل الصدقة لغني ).
واعلم أنه لا يجوز دفعها إلى ثمانية:
الغني، وولد الغني الصغير، وزوجة الغني إذا كان لها مهر عليه، وعبدِ الغني القن، ودفعها إلى ولده وولد ولده وأبويه، وأجداده، وأحد الزوجين إلى الآخر، وبني هاشم والكافر، سواء كان ذمياً أو حربياً. فقوله إلى غني: يعني غنياً يمكنه الانتفاع بماله، حتى لا يدخل عليه ابن السبيل.
فاضلاً
والغني هو من يملك نصاباً من النقدين، أو ما قيمته نصاب، عن حوائجه الأصلية من ثيابه ودار سكناه، وأثاثه، وعبيد خدمته، ودواب ركوبه، وسلاح استعماله.
ثم الغنى على ضربين :
غنى يُحرم عليه طلب الصدقة، وقبولها.
And a mosque is not built with it. And a deceased person is not shrouded with it. Chapter on who it is permissible to give charity to, and who is not permissible. According to the two (Imams), it is permissible to give it to a dhimmi, but giving it to poor Muslims is better. According to Abu Yusuf: it is not permissible; by analogy with zakat. As for a harbi musta'min, it is not permissible to give zakat and obligatory charity to him, by consensus. And it is permissible to give voluntary charity to him. His statement: (And a mosque is not built with it, and a deceased person is not shrouded with it) because of the absence of ownership transfer from it, and that is the pillar. And the proof that ownership transfer is not realized in shrouding the deceased is that if a wolf eats the deceased, the shroud belongs to the one who shrouded, not to the heir. Likewise in al-Nihayah. And likewise the debt of a deceased person is not paid with it. And water stations are not built with it, nor wells dug. And it is not valid unless a poor person takes possession of it, or a guardian or agent takes possession for him; because it is ownership transfer, and taking possession is necessary in it, and for this reason it is not permissible to feed it by way of permission. And if he pays off the debt of a living person: if it is without his command: it is not permissible; if it is with his command: it is permissible if he is poor, and it is as if he gave it as charity to him, and the receiver is like an agent for him in receiving the charity. And a slave is not bought with it to be freed. And it is not given to a rich person. His statement: (And) a slave is not bought with it to be freed) because freeing is relinquishing ownership, and it is not ownership transfer. His statement: (And it is not given to a rich person) because of his statement, peace be upon him: 'Charity is not permissible for a rich person.' And know that it is not permissible to give it to eight: the rich, the young child of the rich, the wife of the rich if she has a dowry against him, the owned slave of the rich, giving it to his child and his child's child and his parents and his grandparents, and one spouse to the other, and Banu Hashim, and the disbeliever, whether dhimmi or harbi. So his statement 'to a rich person' means a rich person who can benefit from his wealth, so that ibn al-sabil is not included. And the rich person is one who possesses a nisab of gold or silver, or something worth a nisab, beyond his basic needs such as his clothes, his residence, his furniture, his servants for service, his riding animals, and his weapons for use. Then wealth is of two types: wealth that prohibits him from asking for charity and accepting it.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira is an expansion (sharh) on al-Mukhtasar al-Quduri, explaining the chapter on who may receive sadaqah. The author begins by reiterating two specific prohibitions: sadaqah cannot be used to build a mosque or to shroud a deceased person. The reason given is that the essence (rukn) of sadaqah is tamlik (transfer of ownership), and these actions do not involve transferring ownership to a recipient. This is supported by the example of a wolf eating the deceased: the shroud belongs to the person who performed the shrouding, not the heir, proving that ownership is not transferred to the deceased. The author then discusses an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding giving sadaqah to a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen). According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, as 'عندهما' typically refers to these two), it is permissible but better to give to poor Muslims. According to Abu Yusuf, it is not permissible, drawing an analogy with zakat. The text then states by consensus that obligatory charity (zakat and obligatory sadaqah) cannot be given to a harbi musta'min (a non-Muslim who has been granted safe passage), but voluntary sadaqah can be. The author continues that sadaqah cannot be used to pay off a deceased person's debt, build water stations or dig wells, because these do not involve tamlik. Valid payment requires that a poor person physically takes possession (qabd), either directly or through a guardian or agent. This is why feeding someone without transferring ownership is not valid. If sadaqah is used to pay off a living person's debt, it is valid only if that person is poor and has authorized the payment. The prohibition also extends to buying a slave to free, because freeing is isqat al-milk (relinquishing ownership), not tamlik. Finally, the author lists eight categories of people who cannot receive sadaqah: the rich, their young child, their wife if owed a dowry, their owned slave, direct descendants and ancestors, spouses to each other, Banu Hashim, and all disbelievers. The definition of rich (ghani) is someone who possesses a nisab of gold or silver (or equivalent value) beyond essential needs. Wealth is then divided into two types: one that prohibits asking for and accepting sadaqah.

Key Terms
تمليك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership of the charity item to the recipient; considered the essential pillar (rukn) of sadaqah according to the author.
قبض (qabd): Physical or constructive possession taken by the recipient; a necessary condition for the validity of sadaqah.
صدقة (sadaqah): Voluntary charity given as ownership transfer to a beneficiary; distinguished from zakat in this passage by context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it not permissible to buy a slave to free with sadaqah?
A) Because freeing a slave is a form of worship, not charity.
B) Because freeing a slave is relinquishment of ownership (isqat al-milk), not transfer of ownership (tamlik).
C) Because a slave is considered property and cannot receive charity directly.
D) Because buying and freeing a slave is spending wealth in a way prohibited by the Prophet.

Key Takeaway
Sadaqah must be given as a transfer of ownership to a living eligible recipient; any use that does not involve tamlik is invalid.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Prohibited Recipients of Sadaqah and the Dhimmi Dispute
Listing prohibited recipients of sadaqah and intra-Hanafi dispute on dhimmis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the eight categories of people who cannot receive sadaqah and explain the intra-Hanafi difference on giving voluntary sadaqah to a dhimmi.

Core Idea
Sadaqah cannot be given to the rich, Banu Hashim, non-Muslims (obligatory), and close relatives; Abu Hanifa allows voluntary sadaqah to dhimmis but Abu Yusuf forbids it.

This passage continues by specifying who cannot receive sadaqah. It lists eight categories, including the rich, close relatives, Banu Hashim, and non-Muslims. It also records an important disagreement within the Hanafi school: while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani permit giving voluntary sadaqah to a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen), Abu Yusuf forbids it, based on analogy with zakat. Understanding these categories ensures that sadaqah is given correctly and avoids prohibited expenditures.

Guided Path
1
Identify the eight prohibited categories
List the eight categories mentioned: rich, young child of rich, wife of rich with mahr, slave of rich, descendants/ancestors, spouses, Banu Hashim, and disbelievers (dhimmi and harbi).
The categories are not all mutually exclusive; they cover different scenarios.
2
Define the 'ghani' (rich person)
A ghani is one who possesses a nisab of gold or silver (or equivalent value) beyond essential needs like clothing, residence, furniture, servants, riding animals, and weapons.
Essential needs are not calculated in the nisab.
3
Examine the dhimmi dispute
State the two positions: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad allow giving voluntary sadaqah to a dhimmi; Abu Yusuf does not, by qiyas on zakat.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze the proof for each side
Abu Hanifa relies on general permissibility (Quran 60:8). Abu Yusuf uses analogy (qiyas) to zakat, which is not given to non-Muslims.
The Hanafi response is that zakat has specific categories; voluntary sadaqah is broader.
5
Understand the consensus on harbi musta'min
By consensus, obligatory sadaqah cannot be given to a harbi musta'min, but voluntary sadaqah can be given.
The distinction between wajib and nafl is crucial.

Key Terms
تمليك (tamlik): Transfer of ownership of the charity item to the recipient; considered the essential pillar (rukn) of sadaqah according to the author.
غني (ghani): A person who possesses a nisab of gold or silver (or equivalent value) beyond essential needs such as clothing, residence, furniture, servants, riding animals, and weapons.
صدقة (sadaqah): Voluntary charity given as ownership transfer to a beneficiary; distinguished from zakat in this passage by context.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim citizen of the Islamic state who is protected and lives under Muslim rule.
حربي مستأمن (harbi musta'min): A non-Muslim from a hostile territory who has been granted safe passage (aman) into Muslim lands.

Zakat — Almsgiving
