Mistaken Zakat Payment: When Intention Suffices
Ruling on zakat given to a mistakenly thought eligible recipient, with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat given mistakenly to an ineligible recipient and explain the conditions under which it is valid.

Core Idea
A sincere intention and reasonable investigation makes zakat valid even if the recipient is later found ineligible.

In this passage, we examine a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens when you give zakat to someone you honestly believe is poor, but later discover they are rich, a Hashimi, a non-Muslim, or even your own relative? Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that your zakat is valid – no need to give again. Abu Yusuf disagrees, requiring repetition. Understanding this ruling hinges on the concept of taharri (genuine investigation) and the weight given to the payer's intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: if one gives zakat to someone mistakenly thought poor (rich, Hashimi, kafir, father/son), the zakat is valid and no re-giving required.
This applies when the payer had taharri and his dominant opinion was that the recipient was eligible.
2
Identify the opposing view (Abu Yusuf)
Abu Yusuf holds that the zakat is invalid and must be repeated because the mistake is clear and could have been avoided.
His reasoning is based on the certainty of error and the possibility of knowing the true status.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Examine the hadith of Yazid bin Ma'n: the Prophet said 'for you what you intended,' indicating intention justifies the validity despite the mistake.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning (dalala) is considered qati in this context.
4
Understand the limits of the dispute
Note that if the recipient is one's own slave or mukatib, all agree zakat is invalid. Also, the ruling only applies when the payer conducted taharri; without it, the zakat is not valid.
The case of parents, children, and wife has a separate narration from Abu Hanifa deeming it invalid.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: no re-giving required, based on the hadith and the principle that intention and due diligence suffice.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال أبو حنيفة ومحمد : إذا دفع الزكاة إلى رجل يظنُّه فقيراً، ثم بـان أنه غني، أو هاشمي، أو كافر، أو دَفَع في ظلمة إلى فقير، ثم بان أنه أبوه، أو ابنه : فلا إعادة عليه . وقال أبو يوسف : عليه الإعادة . ولو دفع إلى شخص، ثم عَلِم أنه عبده، أو مكاتبه : لم يَجُز في قولهم جميعاً . هذا إذا تحرى ودفع وأكثر رأيه أنه مصرِفٌ. أما إذا شك ولم يتحرَّ، أو تحرى ودفع وفي أكثر رأيه أنه ليس بمصرف لا يجزيه إلا إذا علم أنه فقير، وهو الصحيح. وروى ابن شجاع عن أبي حنيفة : أنه لا يجوز في الوالدين والولد والزوجة. كذا في الينابيع». * قوله : أو كافر يعني الذمي، أما الحربي: فلا يجوز. قوله: (وقال أبو يوسف : لا يجوز، وعليه الإعادة)؛ لظهور خطئه بيقين، وإمكان الوقوف على هذه الأشياء. ولهما: ما روي أن يزيد بن معن دفع صدقته إلى رجل، وأمره أن يتصدق بها، فدفعها إلى أبيه ليلاً، فلما أصبح رآها معه في يده، فاختصما إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال يا يزيد ! لك ما نويت، ولك يا معن ما أخذت . * قوله: (ولو دفع إلى شخص يظنه فقيراً، ثم بان أنه عبده أو مكاتبه : لم يجز، في قولهم جميعاً)؛ لأنهما ملكه، فلا يتحقق التمليك؛ لعدم أهلية الملك.
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad said: If one gives zakat to a man thinking he is poor, then it becomes apparent that he is rich, or a Hashimi, or a disbeliever, or if he gives in the dark to a poor person, then it becomes apparent that he is his father or his son, then he does not have to repeat. Abu Yusuf said: He must repeat. If he gives to a person, then learns that he is his slave or his mukatib, it is not valid according to all of them. This is when he investigates and gives, and his predominant opinion is that he is an eligible recipient. But if he doubts and does not investigate, or investigates and gives while his predominant opinion is that he is not eligible, it does not suffice unless he knows he is poor, and that is the correct view. Ibn Shuja' narrated from Abu Hanifa that it is not valid regarding parents, children, and the wife. This is in al-Yanabi'. * His statement: 'or a disbeliever' means a dhimmi, as for a harbi, it is not valid. His statement: (Abu Yusuf said: it is not valid, and he must repeat) because his mistake became clearly apparent, and it is possible to have known these things. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) there is the narration that Yazid bin Ma'n gave his zakat to a man and instructed him to give it in charity, so he gave it to his father at night. In the morning he saw it with him in his hand, and they went to the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: O Yazid, for you what you intended, and O Ma'n, for you what you took. * His statement: (If he gives to a person thinking he is poor, then it becomes apparent that he is his slave or mukatib, it is not valid according to all of them) because they are his property, so ownership is not achieved due to lack of capacity for ownership.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the validity of zakat when given to a person mistakenly thought to be eligible. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that if one gives zakat under the mistaken belief that the recipient is poor (but later turns out to be rich, Hashimi, or a disbeliever), or if he gives in the dark to a poor person who then turns out to be his father or son, the zakat is valid and no re-giving is required. Abu Yusuf disagrees, requiring re-giving. The text then provides additional rulings: all three agree that if the recipient is later found to be one's own slave or mukatib, the zakat is invalid because the recipient lacks the capacity to own property relative to the giver (as the slave's property belongs to the master). The commentator explains that these rulings apply only when the giver has made a genuine effort to investigate (taharri) and his dominant opinion was that the person was eligible. If he gave without investigation or despite thinking the person was ineligible, the zakat is not valid unless he knew for sure. A narration from Ibn Shuja' reports that Abu Hanifa also rules that giving to one's parents, children, or wife is invalid. The proof for Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's position is the hadith of Yazid bin Ma'n, who delegated someone to distribute his zakat, and that person gave it to his own father. The Prophet ruled that the delegator (Yazid) gets reward for his intention, and the son (Ma'n) keeps what he took, implying the zakat was valid without re-giving. Abu Yusuf's position is based on the clear mistake and the possibility of having known the true status. The Hanafi response (wa lahuma) relies on the hadith, which shows that even when the recipient turned out to be the agent's own father (who is normally prohibited from receiving zakat), the zakat was valid, so by analogy, other mistaken cases are also valid.

Key Terms
تحرى (taharri): Making a genuine effort to determine the eligibility of the zakat recipient before giving.
مكاتب (mukatib): A slave who has a contract to purchase his freedom. Giving zakat to one's own mukatib is invalid because he is still under ownership.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under Muslim protection. The passage says 'kaafir' means dhimmi; giving zakat to a dhimmi mistakenly is governed by the same dispute.
هاشمي (Hashimi): A descendant of Hashim, the Prophet's clan. Zakat is prohibited to them because they are entitled to khums and other funds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, if someone gives zakat to a person he thinks is poor but later discovers the person is rich, what is the ruling?
A) The zakat is invalid and must be given again
B) The zakat is valid and no re-giving is required
C) The zakat is valid only if the recipient returns the money
D) The zakat becomes a voluntary charity (sadaqah)

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, if a zakat-payer made a genuine effort (taharri) to determine eligibility, the zakat is valid even if the recipient is later found ineligible.

Zakat to One's Own Slave: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Repetition
Intra-Hanafi dispute on repetition of zakat paid to one's own slave/mukatab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on paying zakat to one's own slave or mukatab, identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Yusuf and the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and apply the condition of taharrī to determine validity.

Core Idea
When zakat is mistakenly paid to one's own slave, validity hinges on genuine ijtihad—Abu Yusuf demands repetition; Abu Hanifa and Muhammad accept intention.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar addresses a critical scenario: a person pays zakat to someone he later discovers is his own slave or mukatab. The Hanafi imams agree the payment is fundamentally invalid in such a case, but they differ on whether the discoverer must repeat the payment. The resolution lies in a nuanced principle: the role of taharrī (exerting effort to identify a valid recipient) and the weight of intention (niyyah).

Guided Path
1
State the agreed ruling
All Hanafi imams agree that paying zakat to one's own slave or mukatab is invalid (batil) because the recipient lacks capacity to own from the payer.
This is the baseline: the act itself is invalid regardless of intention.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that the payer must repeat the payment (i'ādah) because the error is clear and could have been avoided. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that if the payer made taharrī and his predominant opinion was that the recipient was eligible, the payment is valid and no repetition is needed.
The ikhtilaf centers on the role of the payer's due diligence and intention.
3
Follow Abu Yusuf's dalil
Abu Yusuf argues that since the mistake is manifest (e.g., paying one's own slave) and ascertainable beforehand, the payment is void and must be redone.
His reasoning is based on the possibility of avoiding the error.
4
Follow the dalil of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad)
They cite the hadith of Yazid ibn Ma'n where the Prophet (ﷺ) said 'for you is what you intended' (lakā mā nawayta). This indicates that sincere intention can validate the charity even if the recipient turns out to be a near relative.
The hadith is found in Sahih al-Bukhari (no. 1422).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text says 'wa huwa al-sahih' (this is correct) referring to the condition of taharrī, implying that the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
Thus, in practice, if the payer made a genuine effort, his zakat is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال أبو يوسف : عليه الإعادة . باب من يجوز دفع الصدقة إليه، ومن لا يجوز ولو دفع إلى شخص، ثم عَلِم أنه عبده، أو مكاتبه : لم يَجُز في قولهم جميعاً . هذا إذا تحرى ودفع وأكثر رأيه أنه مصرِفٌ. أما إذا شك ولم يتحرَّ، أو تحرى ودفع وفي أكثر رأيه أنه ليس بمصرف لا يجزيه إلا إذا علم أنه فقير، وهو الصحيح. وروى ابن شجاع عن أبي حنيفة : أنه لا يجوز في الوالدين والولد والزوجة. كذا في الينابيع». * قوله : أو كافر يعني الذمي، أما الحربي: فلا يجوز. قوله: (وقال أبو يوسف : لا يجوز، وعليه الإعادة)؛ لظهور خطئه بيقين، وإمكان الوقوف على هذه الأشياء. ولهما: ما روي أن يزيد بن معن دفع صدقته إلى رجل، وأمره أن يتصدق بها، فدفعها إلى أبيه ليلاً، فلما أصبح رآها معه في يده، فاختصما إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال يا يزيد ! لك ما نويت، ولك يا معن ما أخذت (۱) : * قوله: (ولو دفع إلى شخص يظنه فقيراً، ثم بان أنه عبده أو مكاتبه : لم يجز، في قولهم جميعاً)؛ لأنهما ملكه، فلا يتحقق التمليك؛ لعدم أهلية الملك. (۱) صحيح البخاري (١٤٢٢).
And Abu Yusuf said: He must repeat (the payment). Chapter: Who is Permitted to Give Charity (Zakat) to, and Who is Not. If he pays to a person, then learns that he is his slave or mukatab: it is not valid according to all of them. This is if he has exerted effort (taharrā) and paid while his predominant opinion was that he is a valid recipient. As for if he doubted and did not exert effort, or he exerted effort and paid while his predominant opinion was that he is not a valid recipient, it does not suffice him unless he knows that he is poor, and this is the correct ruling. And Ibn Shujā' narrated from Abu Hanifa: that it is not valid regarding parents, children, and wife. Likewise in al-Yanābī'. His statement: 'or a disbeliever' means the dhimmī; as for the harbī, it is not valid. His statement: (And Abu Yusuf said: It is not valid, and he must repeat) because his error is clearly known and it is possible to ascertain these matters. And for them (the two - Abu Hanifa and Muhammad): it is narrated that Yazīd ibn Ma'n gave his charity to a man, and ordered him to give it in charity, so he gave it to his father at night. When morning came, he saw it with him in his hand, so they brought their dispute to the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, and he said: 'O Yazīd, for you is what you intended, and for you O Ma'n is what you took.' (1) His statement: (If he pays to a person he thinks is poor, then it becomes clear that he is his slave or his mukatab: it is not valid, according to all of them) because they are his property, so ownership is not realized due to lack of capacity for ownership. (1) Sahīh al-Bukhārī (1422).
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is from a commentary on Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, discussing when zakat payment is invalid. The core ruling: if a person pays his zakat to someone he later discovers is his own slave or mukatab, the payment is invalid according to all Hanafi imams. The commentary then distinguishes cases based on the payer's ijtihad (taharrī). If he made a genuine effort and his predominant opinion was that the recipient was eligible, the payment is valid (i.e., no need to repeat). If he was negligent or his predominant opinion was against eligibility, the payment is not sufficient unless he later confirms the recipient was actually poor. A separate narration from Abu Hanifa extends this to parents, children, and wife: payment to them is also invalid. The commentary also clarifies that 'disbeliever' (kāfir) refers to a dhimmi—paying zakat to a harbi is invalid. An intra-Hanafi dispute arises: Abu Yusuf holds that if the error is clear (e.g., paying to one's own slave), the payment must be repeated because the mistake is obvious and could have been avoided. The two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) rely on a hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) said 'for you is what you intended,' indicating that valid intention (niyyah) suffices even if the recipient turns out to be a relative, so no repetition is needed. The commentary then restates the ruling on slaves and mukatab: invalidity due to lack of ownership capacity.

Key Terms
مصرف (masrif): A valid recipient of zakat, someone eligible to receive the payment.
تحرى (taharrā): Exerting effort to determine the eligibility of a potential zakat recipient.
مكاتب (mukātab): A slave who has entered into a contract of manumission (kitābah) with his master, agreeing to pay a sum for freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the hadith cited by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad to support their view, what did the Prophet (ﷺ) say to Yazid ibn Ma'n?
A) 'You must repeat the charity.'
B) 'For you is what you intended.'
C) 'The charity is invalid.'
D) 'You have sinned.'

Key Takeaway
Zakat paid to one's own property is invalid, but if the payer made genuine ijtihad (taharrī), the relied-upon Hanafi view holds the payment valid and does not require repetition.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Recipient Conditions and Large Sums in Zakat
Explains that zakat cannot be given to a nisab owner and the dislike of giving large sums to one poor person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid zakat recipient according to the Hanafi school and explain the ruling (makruh tanzih) on giving 200 dirhams or more to a single poor person, including the ikhtilaf with Zufar.

Core Idea
Zakat cannot be given to a nisab owner; giving 200 dirhams to one poor person is valid but makruh.

This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayirah addresses two important issues for zakat distribution: who is eligible to receive zakat, and how much may be given to a single recipient. The first part clarifies that a recipient must not own a nisab of any wealth, even non-productive assets. The second part discusses the ruling on giving large sums—such as 200 dirhams or more—to one poor person, where the majority Hanafi position deems it makruh tanzih yet valid, contrary to Zufar's view of invalidity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Recipient's Condition
The passage states: you cannot give zakat to someone who owns a nisab (minimum threshold) from any wealth. Understand what constitutes a nisab (200 dirhams of silver or equivalent) and that it must be surplus to basic needs.
Even a house not lived in worth 200 dirhams disqualifies the owner from receiving zakat.
2
Apply the Nisab Rule to Various Cases
Consider the example from al-Marghinani: a person owns five camels worth less than 200 dirhams—he is eligible to receive zakat, and also obligated to pay zakat on the camels. This shows the criterion is the cash nisab, not the type of wealth owned.
The nisab of currency (naqd) is the standard, regardless of the kind of property.
3
Examine the Ruling on Giving a Large Amount
The passage says it is disliked (makruh) to give 200 dirhams or more to a single poor person, but if done, it is valid. Understand why: it potentially makes the recipient wealthy at that moment, but the zakat obligation is still fulfilled.
The dislike is tanzihi (light dislike), not tahrimi.
4
Evaluate Zufar's Dissent
Zufar argues it is invalid because the recipient becomes wealthy at the moment of payment. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold validity. Note the practical difference: under Zufar, the giver would have to repeat zakat if he gave 200 or more; under the majority, no repetition is needed.
The mufta bihi position is validity with dislike.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب من يجوز دفع الصدقة إليه، ومن لا يجوز ولا يجوز دفع الزكاة إلى من يملك نصاباً من أي مال كان . ويجوز دفعها إلى مَن يملك أقل من ذلك وإن كان صحيحاً مكتسباً. وكذا إذا كان مدبَّره أو أم ولده : لا يجزيه، ويلزمه الإعادة. * قوله: (ولا يجوز دَفْعُ الزكاة إلى مَن يَملك نصاباً من أي مال كان). وسواء كان النصاب نامياً أو غير نام حتى لو كان له بيت لا يسكنه يساوي مائتي درهم: لا يجوز صرف الزكاة إليه. وهذا النصاب المعتبر في وجوب الفطرة، والأضحية. قال في المرغيناني: إذا كان له خمس من الإبل قيمتها أقل من مائتي درهم: تحل له الزكاة، وتجب عليه. ولهذا يظهر أن المعتبر : نصاب النقد من أي مال كان بلغ نصاباً من جنسه، أو لم يبلغ. وقوله : إلى من يملك نصاباً بشرط أن يكون النصاب فاضلاً عن حوائجه الأصلية. قوله: (ويجوز دفعها إلى من يملك أقل من ذلك وإن كان صحيحاً مكتسباً) ؛ لأنه فقير، إلا أنه يحرم عليه السؤال. ويكره أن يدفع إلى فقير واحد مائتي درهم فصاعداً، فإن دفع: جاز. وقال زفر : لا يجوز؛ لأن الغنى قارن الأداء، فحصل الأداء إلى الغني.
Chapter: Who is Permitted to Give Charity (Zakat) to, and Who is Not. It is not permitted to give zakat to someone who owns a nisab from any wealth. And it is permitted to give it to someone who owns less than that, even if he is healthy and earning a living. Likewise, if he is a mudabbir (a slave whose manumission is delayed after the master's death) or a slave-mother (umm walad): it does not suffice him, and he must repeat. * His statement: (It is not permitted to give zakat to someone who owns a nisab from any wealth). Whether the nisab is productive or not, even if he owns a house that he does not live in worth two hundred dirhams, it is not permissible to give zakat to him. And this nisab is considered for the obligation of fitrah and sacrifice. Al-Marghinani said: If he has five camels whose value is less than two hundred dirhams, zakat is permissible for him, and it is obligatory upon him. Thus it appears that the consideration is the nisab of currency (naqd) from whatever wealth, whether it reaches a nisab of its kind or not. And his statement: 'to someone who owns a nisab' with the condition that the nisab is surplus to his basic needs. His statement: (And it is permitted to give it to someone who owns less than that even if he is healthy and earning a living) because he is poor, but it is forbidden for him to beg. It is disliked to give a single poor person two hundred dirhams or more; if he gives, it is valid. And Zufar said: It is not valid because wealth accompanied the payment, so the payment was made to a wealthy person.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage continues the same chapter, now addressing two key issues: (1) the condition of the recipient's wealth, and (2) the amount given to a single recipient. First, zakat cannot be given to anyone who owns a nisab (minimum wealth threshold) from any type of property. The nisab considered is that of currency (200 dirhams or equivalent of gold/silver). It does not matter if the property is productive (like trade goods) or non-productive (like an unused house). The nisab must be surplus to basic needs (e.g., one's dwelling, clothing, furniture). A quote from al-Marghinani clarifies that if a person owns five camels worth less than 200 dirhams, they are eligible to receive zakat (despite owning the camels, because the value is below the nisab). Second, it is permissible to give zakat to a person who owns less than a nisab, even if he is healthy and able to work, because he is still poor (faqir). However, it is forbidden for such a person to beg (the sin is on him, not the giver). Lastly, there is a ruling on giving a large amount: it is disliked (makruh) to give 200 dirhams or more to a single poor person, because it might make him wealthy and remove his eligibility. But if one does so, the payment is valid and his zakat obligation is fulfilled. Zufar disagreed, arguing that at the moment of payment the recipient becomes wealthy, so the payment is invalid. The relied-upon position is that it is valid but disliked (makruh tanzihi).

Key Terms
نصاب (nisāb): The minimum amount of wealth that makes a person liable to pay zakat (if he owns it) or makes him ineligible to receive zakat (if he owns it).
مدبر (mudabbir): A slave whose master has declared that he will be free after the master's death.
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has given birth to a child from her master, and becomes free upon the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on giving 200 dirhams or more to a single poor person?
A) Permissible without any dislike
B) Disliked (makruh) but valid
C) Invalid because the recipient becomes wealthy
D) Obligatory to give that amount

Key Takeaway
Zakat cannot be given to a nisab owner; giving 200 dirhams or more to a single poor person is valid but makruh tanzih.

Zakat — Almsgiving
beginner
8 min
Who May Receive Zakat: The Nisab Condition
States the ruling with commentary on nisab condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of nisab for zakat recipients and apply it to determine who is eligible to receive zakat.

Core Idea
Zakat cannot be given to anyone who owns a complete nisab — but it can be given to a healthy earner who owns less.

In this passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, the commentator expands on al-Quduri's matn regarding the eligibility of zakat recipients. The key principle is that ownership of a nisab (minimum zakatable threshold) disqualifies a person from receiving zakat, regardless of the type of property. However, one who owns less than a nisab is eligible, even if they are physically able to earn. This lesson unpacks the nisab condition and its nuances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Category
The act under discussion is giving zakat to a recipient. This is an act of worship (ibadah) with specific conditions for validity.
Zakat is a wajib act; improper delivery renders it invalid.
2
Identify the Hukm Level for Improper Recipient
The matn states that giving zakat to one who owns a nisab is not permissible (la yajuz) and does not suffice (la yujzi), requiring repetition.
The hukm level is batil: the payment is void and must be repeated.
3
List the Conditions for a Valid Recipient
The primary condition is that the recipient must not own a full nisab of any property after excluding basic necessities. The commentary clarifies that the nisab considered is that of currency (200 dirhams silver equivalent) and that the nisab must be surplus to the recipient's basic needs.
Basic needs include a residence, household goods, etc.
4
Note What Invalidates the Payment
In addition to giving to a nisab-owner, giving zakat to one's own mudabbar or umm walad does not suffice and must be repeated.
This is because the giver has a right of ownership over them.
5
Examine the Commentary's Expansion on Nisab
The commentator provides examples: a house not lived in worth 200 dirhams disqualifies; five camels valued under 200 dirhams do not disqualify. The key is the value in silver dirhams.
Al-Marghinani's statement reinforces that the nisab of currency is the standard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب من يجوز دفع الصدقة إليه، ومن لا يجوز
ولا يجوز دفع الزكاة إلى من يملك نصاباً من أي مال كان . ويجوز دفعها إلى مَن يملك أقل من ذلك وإن كان صحيحاً مكتسباً.
وكذا إذا كان مدبَّره أو أم ولده : لا يجزيه، ويلزمه الإعادة. * قوله: (ولا يجوز دَفْعُ الزكاة إلى مَن يَملك نصاباً من أي مال كان). سواء كان النصاب نامياً أو غير نام حتى لو كان له بيت لا يسكنه يساوي مائتي درهم: لا يجوز صرف الزكاة إليه.
وهذا النصاب المعتبر في وجوب الفطرة، والأضحية.
قال في المرغيناني: إذا كان له خمس من الإبل قيمتها أقل من مائتي درهم: تحل له الزكاة، وتجب عليه.
ولهذا يظهر أن المعتبر : نصاب النقد من أي مال كان بلغ نصاباً من جنسه، أو لم يبلغ.
وقوله : إلى من يملك نصاباً بشرط أن يكون النصاب فاضلاً عن حوائجه الأصلية.
قوله: (ويجوز دفعها إلى من يملك أقل من ذلك وإن كان صحيحاً مكتسباً) ؛ لأنه فقير، إلا أنه يحرم عليه السؤال.
Chapter: Who may be given charity and who may not be given. It is not permissible to pay zakat to one who owns a nisab of any property. It is permissible to pay it to one who owns less than that, even if he is healthy and earning. Likewise, if it is his mudabbar or umm walad: it does not suffice him, and he must repeat. * His statement: (It is not permissible to pay zakat to one who owns a nisab of any property). Whether the nisab is growing or non-growing, even if he has a house he does not live in worth two hundred dirhams: it is not permissible to pay zakat to him. This nisab is the same considered for the obligation of fitrah and sacrifice. Al-Marghinani said: If he has five camels whose value is less than two hundred dirhams, zakat is permissible for him and obligatory upon him. Hence it appears that the consideration is the nisab of currency, from any property, whether it reaches the nisab of its own type or not. His statement: 'to one who owns a nisab' with the condition that the nisab is surplus over his basic needs. His statement: (It is permissible to pay it to one who owns less than that, even if he is healthy and earning) because he is poor, except that it is forbidden for him to ask.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of al-Quduri, expanded by the commentator. It establishes two core rules: (1) Zakat cannot be given to anyone who possesses a full nisab (minimum wealth threshold) of any type of property. The nisab considered is the nisab of currency (200 dirhams of silver or equivalent), regardless of whether the property itself is of that type or not. The nisab must be surplus to the recipient's basic needs (like a residence). (2) Zakat may be given to someone who owns less than a nisab, even if they are healthy and able to earn, because they are considered poor (faqir). However, it is haram for such a person to beg. The commentator also notes an additional ruling: if the recipient is the giver's mudabbar (a slave promised freedom upon the master's death) or umm walad (a slave mother of the master's child), the payment does not count and must be repeated.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisāb): The minimum amount of wealth that makes a person liable to pay zakat, and that disqualifies a person from receiving zakat.
فقير (faqīr): A person who owns less than a nisab, even if healthy and earning, making them eligible to receive zakat.
مدبَّر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death.
أم ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master, becoming free upon his death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Is it permissible to give zakat to a person who owns a house worth 300 dirhams that he lives in, but has no other wealth?
A) Yes, because the house is a basic need and not surplus to nisab.
B) No, because the house exceeds 200 dirhams.
C) Yes, because he can sell the house.
D) No, because he is not earning.

Key Takeaway
A person is eligible to receive zakat if they do not own a nisab of wealth surplus to basic needs, regardless of health or earning ability.
